  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_4303fe35-2679-476b-94a0-113bb7ddec2a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/3446-i-m-sorta-a-happy-ending-girl-i-ve">I&#39;m sorta a happy ending girl. I&#39;ve started reading some spooky books like &quot;The Cavandish home for Boys and Girls&quot; and &quot;The books of Elsewhere&quot; and I&#39;d like to try this one. I don&#39;t mind blood, just not gore and a little bit of scary stuff is ok. How dark is this book? I don&#39;t want to read it only to scare me half to death.</a>
</div>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">This book is not for people with weak tolerance for death, blood, and overall gore. The ending is fairly happy, but VERY bloody things happen on the w<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">This book is not for people with weak tolerance for death, blood, and overall gore. The ending is fairly happy, but VERY bloody things happen on the way. The book is very good, though. There are 'warnings' about when blood is coming. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1060786770957454369"><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567310888i/28081968._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <br/>
  <br/>
  <i>Once upon a time, fairy tales were AWESOME!</i>
</blockquote>Adam Gidwitz remembers the old tales - <b>the ones with violence and blood -</b> and truly regrets the watering down the modern times.<br/><br/>And so he decides to tell the true tale of Hansel and Gretel.<br/><br/>Their story is not all <b>gingerbread and breadcrumbs </b>- there's vampires, werewolves and monsters galore. <br/><br/>There will be trials, tribulations and betrayal. <br/><br/> They each die at least once.<blockquote>
  <i>"You're being foolish," Gretel told herself. "Rain can't talk."<br/><br/>No, of co</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText1060786770957454369" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567310888i/28081968._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <br>
  <i>Once upon a time, fairy tales were AWESOME!</i>
</blockquote>Adam Gidwitz remembers the old tales - <b>the ones with violence and blood -</b> and truly regrets the watering down the modern times.<br><br>And so he decides to tell the true tale of Hansel and Gretel.<br><br>Their story is not all <b>gingerbread and breadcrumbs </b>- there's vampires, werewolves and monsters galore. <br><br>There will be trials, tribulations and betrayal. <br><br> They each die at least once.<blockquote>
  <i>"You're being foolish," Gretel told herself. "Rain can't talk."<br><br>No, of course it can't. The moon can eat children, and fingers can open doors, and people's heads can be put back on.<br>But rain? Talk? Don't be ridiculous.</i>
</blockquote> They have <b>a kingdom that needs saving</b> and they are ready to do something about it.<blockquote>
  <i>There is a wisdom in children, a kind of knowing, a kind of believing, that we, as adults, do not have. There is a time when a kingdom needs its children.</i>
</blockquote>Will they be able to save the entire kingdom in time? <b>
  <i>Or will they lose everything they've ever known?</i>
</b><br><br>Overall, I liked this one!<br><br> It was fun and funny, though at times it seemed to try too hard to insert humor by <b>breaking the fourth wall.</b><br><br>I did enjoy how Gidwitz took all the old tales and told them in a fresh and fabulous way.<br><br>Hansel and Gretel developed quite nicely from<b> timid children into heroes. </b><br><br>It was quite interesting to follow along on their adventures.<br><br> The stories did have a slight old-timey feel (ie lots of magic just happens without explanation) but the author balanced it well enough with the plot that I wasn't bothered by it too much. <br><br>I never knew what direction this book was going but the journey was a great adventure.<br><br><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br>Read by Johnny Heller and it was great to listen to. Loved it!!<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!<br></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mischenko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mischenko" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko">Mischenko</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1991605777" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13053260343402008793">To see this review and others please visit <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.readrantrockandroll.com'>www.readrantrockandroll.com</a><br/><br/>I have a thing for fairy tales, especially Hansel and Gretel. So when I saw <i>A Tale Dark and Grimm</i> at the library a few weeks ago, I couldn't hesitate. I needed to read this book. <br/><br/>Firstly, I thought the story was incredibly creative. It's like the classic Hansel and Gretel except in addition to the witch, they deal with many other scary beings and they move through different fairy tales. They decide they must choose their own f</span>
  <span id="freeText13053260343402008793" style="display:none">To see this review and others please visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.readrantrockandroll.com">www.readrantrockandroll.com</a><br /><br />I have a thing for fairy tales, especially Hansel and Gretel. So when I saw <i>A Tale Dark and Grimm</i> at the library a few weeks ago, I couldn't hesitate. I needed to read this book. <br /><br />Firstly, I thought the story was incredibly creative. It's like the classic Hansel and Gretel except in addition to the witch, they deal with many other scary beings and they move through different fairy tales. They decide they must choose their own fate and they're trying to locate caretakers that aren't dangerous and brutal toward them. In a nutshell, they're trying to stay alive. In between certain tales and sections we have a narrator that lightens the mood and warns before something violent is about to happen. I liked that, but at times it was also distracting.<br /><br />Secondly, is this seriously Juvenile Fiction for 3rd grade+? It seems way to gruesome for 3rd graders to be reading, but in a way the story is fairly simple which makes me have a love hate relationship with it as far as the reading level. I would put this into the 5-6th grade level, but not 3rd grade and that's based solely on the content. The author is covering Grimm's fairy tales here with added twists and I don't necessarily feel that readers should be spared on the details, but maybe this should be listed for an older audience. It's fairly sadistic at times. I'd say for younger readers it's best to read with an adult.<br /><br />Overall rating on this one is 4****</span>
  <a data-text-id="13053260343402008793" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

Gidwitz weaves the fairy tales together into a single narrative featuring Hansel and Gretel, and does it so well you’ll be wondering if this was the way the stories were meant to be told back </span>
  <span id="freeText12593781670777379545" style="display:none">This debut YA novel is getting a lot of well-deserved attention. Gidwitz manages to balance the grisly violence of the original Grimms’ fairy tales with a wonderful sense of humor and narrative voice, somewhat reminiscent of Lemony Snicket’s take on the penny dreadful, but also completely fresh and unique. Gidwitz weaves the fairy tales together into a single narrative featuring Hansel and Gretel, and does it so well you’ll be wondering if this was the way the stories were meant to be told back in the old days. Check it out!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2980138699" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13746971327524188547">Lemony Snicket walked so this series could run.<br/><br/>Yeah. I said it.<br/><br/>My dear sister dearly loves this book, and so I read it because things that are dear to people who are dear to me should automatically be dear to me too.<br/><br/>Feel like that’s a rule.<br/><br/>This was fine, but a little boring. Which is shocking because I tend to find that middle grade adventure is way less boring than young adult anything. But here we are.<br/><br/>It was very, very dark, which I respect. Extremely dark and gory and violent and borderline-f</span>
  <span id="freeText13746971327524188547" style="display:none">Lemony Snicket walked so this series could run.<br /><br />Yeah. I said it.<br /><br />My dear sister dearly loves this book, and so I read it because things that are dear to people who are dear to me should automatically be dear to me too.<br /><br />Feel like that’s a rule.<br /><br />This was fine, but a little boring. Which is shocking because I tend to find that middle grade adventure is way less boring than young adult anything. But here we are.<br /><br />It was very, very dark, which I respect. Extremely dark and gory and violent and borderline-frightening-even-for-an-adult children’s books? Hardcore. <br /><br />It just didn’t have much other than that? The narrative voice tried, but fell a little flat. The plot was choppy. The characters weren’t much of anything. <br /><br />It was fine, but also in a disappointing way.<br /><br />Bottom line: I’m just going to read A Series of Unfortunate Events and a book of fairytales at the same time and pretend it’s the same thing. <br /><br />------------<br /><br />a list of things i love:<br />- children's books<br />- fairytales<br />- fairytales specifically of the dark and, well, grim variety<br />- snarky narrators<br />- badassery of all kinds<br /><br />this book:<br />- HAS OR IS ALL OF THE ABOVE.</span>

    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/114202615?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781449841249" href="/book/show/11287115-a-tale-dark-and-grimm">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fairy tale lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=fairy-tale-theme">fairy-tale-theme</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=library-checkout">library-checkout</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=middle-grade-juvenile">middle-grade-juvenile</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=not-for-the-faint-of-heart">not-for-the-faint-of-heart</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=2011-reading">2011-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=to-buy-wish-list">to-buy-wish-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=metafiction">metafiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=tortured-hero">tortured-hero</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer114202615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17989342215260863014">I loved, loved, loved this book! This is the kind of book that I wish I could find more of. I think it was a wonderful fix of humor, horror, suspense, angst, and a great coming of age story. I didn't think that I would appreciate a story with Hansel and Gretel thrown into other fairy tales, nor could their story sustain a full-length novel. I was wrong on both counts. Hansel and Gretel became very dear to my hearts. They started out as little children who were doing what little children did. Liv</span>
  <span id="freeText17989342215260863014" style="display:none">I loved, loved, loved this book! This is the kind of book that I wish I could find more of. I think it was a wonderful fix of humor, horror, suspense, angst, and a great coming of age story. I didn't think that I would appreciate a story with Hansel and Gretel thrown into other fairy tales, nor could their story sustain a full-length novel. I was wrong on both counts. Hansel and Gretel became very dear to my hearts. They started out as little children who were doing what little children did. Living their lives, having fun, basking in the love of their parents and caregivers. Until circumstances cause them to embark out into the cold, cruel, scary world.<br /><br />Adam Gidwitz doesn't go easy on Hansel and Gretel, nor does he go easy on the reader. There are some very violent, disturbing aspects in this story. For that reason, I disagree with the 9 and older rating. I would say it should be 11 and older. I realize that he is true to the original Grimm's fairy tales, and I know I did read fairy tales at a younger age. So maybe some kids would be fine with it. As a grown up, I winced on some parts myself. <br /><br />I loved the aspect of the narrator breaching the third wall and talking to the audience as he read. He would warn us to send the little kids to bed or to get the babysitter. He would warn the reader that some very bloody parts were coming, and good thing he did. He would encourage the reader through the very sad parts (and they were very sad). He would make hilarious asides that had me braying with laughter in my car as I listened. My sister told me I was silly when I laughed at some parts yesterday. But it was so funny! This is a truly fun book, guys! And Johnny Heller, the narrator, did such a great job of creating a lively atmosphere for this story. Kudos to him!<br /><br />A Tale Dark and Grimm is a story of courage. It's a novel that shows that children have depths of endurance, ingenuity and strength that adults often dismiss. I'm not saying that every child could survive what Hansel and Gretel endure, but I think about what kids go through every day, and this message resonated with me. It's also a cautionary tale to parents. Parents need to consider carefully what it means to be a parent, and how much they cherish their children. Are children a means to an end, a possession, or are they worth their weight in gold? I'll leave that to people with kids to decide, although I have my own opinions on that.<br /><br />My verdict on this book is as follows: Read it! If you like fairy tales, you definitely need to read it. If you see this on audio at your library, pick it up, just for fun. Although some parts are pretty tough, this was a very entertaining and often moving story. I borrowed this from my library, but I definitely want to get my own copy to add to my keeper shelf, preferably with my fairy tale collection.<br /><br />Highly recommended!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17989342215260863014" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_110820077" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/110820077" />
    <a title="Betsy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/221050-betsy"><img alt="Betsy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442631153p2/221050.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/110820077?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Betsy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Betsy" href="/user/show/221050-betsy">Betsy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110820077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16251806059422881113">Didn’t want to read this. Nope. Not a jot. Three reasons for that. First off, the title. I’ve said it about twenty times since reading it and every time I can’t quite get it right (derivations have included "Something Dark and Grimm", “A Grimm Tale”, and “Something Grimm”). Second, the jacket of the hardcover edition of this book isn’t particularly new. Silhouettes against a blue background. Ho hum. Third, I couldn’t believe that I was dealing with yet ANOTHER middle grade novel adapting fairy t</span>
  <span id="freeText16251806059422881113" style="display:none">Didn’t want to read this. Nope. Not a jot. Three reasons for that. First off, the title. I’ve said it about twenty times since reading it and every time I can’t quite get it right (derivations have included "Something Dark and Grimm", “A Grimm Tale”, and “Something Grimm”). Second, the jacket of the hardcover edition of this book isn’t particularly new. Silhouettes against a blue background. Ho hum. Third, I couldn’t believe that I was dealing with yet ANOTHER middle grade novel adapting fairy tales in new ways. After a while the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/176327.The_Fairy_Tale_Detectives__The_Sisters_Grimm___1_" title="The Fairy-Tale Detectives (The Sisters Grimm, #1) by Michael Buckley" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sisters Grimm</a> / <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6760780.The_Grimm_Legacy" title="The Grimm Legacy by Polly Shulman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Grimm Legacy</a> titles out there begin to meld together. From <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/179064.The_Goose_Girl__The_Books_of_Bayern___1_" title="The Goose Girl (The Books of Bayern, #1) by Shannon Hale" rel="nofollow noopener">The Goose Girl</a> to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/170136.Into_the_Wild" rel="nofollow noopener">Into the Wild</a> to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6357708.Sisters_Red__Sisters_Red___1_" title="Sisters Red (Sisters Red, #1) by Jackson Pearce" rel="nofollow noopener">Sisters Red</a> I sometimes feel as if I am a little tired of fairy tales. I guess it takes a book like <i>A Tale Dark and Grimm</i> to wake me out of this funk. To my surprise, Gidwitz’s debut is unlike anything I’ve ever encountered before. I’ve never seen a book meld the snarky narrator of something like a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/36746.Lemony_Snicket" title="Lemony Snicket" rel="nofollow noopener">Lemony Snicket</a> title so seamlessly with the original tone and telling of the original Grimm fairy tales. And not the sweet tales either. This is a book that isn’t afraid to get to the root of a good story. The fact that it unearths some of the more frightening ones along the way just happens to be a bonus.<br />	<br />We all know some of the better known Grimm fairy tales out there like “Rapunzel” or “Cinderella”. Heck, we probably even know some of their original story elements (chopping of heels and toes, getting blinded by thorns, etc.). The Grimm tales were just that. Grim. Now imagine finding yourself living them. Prince Hansel and Princess Gretel are born in one lesser known Grimm fairy tales, “Faithful Johannes” and when they discover that their mom and dad are potentially unhinged they set off to make their way in the world and find some decent parents. In doing so they wander through a series of little known tales like “The Devil With the Three Golden Hairs” and “The Seven Ravens”. Unfortunately, while doing so they have a tendency to lose digits, lose their humanity, lose their lives (almost), and find that sometimes the fastest way to end your travels to go back to where you started. <br />	<br />There are times in a children’s librarian’s life when it is very useful to own the third edition of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6512309-the-complete-fairy-tales-of-the-brothers-grimm" rel="nofollow noopener">The Complete Fairy Tales of the Brothers Grimm </a> as translated by Jack Zipes (who, by the way, blurbed this book). You just never know when you might need such a book. In this particular case I decided to inspect the stories Gidwitz appropriated to see exactly how closely they adhered to the originals. I was not disappointed. “Faithful Johannes”? Dead on, including the whole kidnapping the mom bit. "The Devil With the Three Golden Hairs"? At points, nearly word for word. He's often faithful, but sometimes I wondered if Gidwitz was calling upon versions of tales even older than the Grimm’s. The fact that the witch in the story “Hansel and Gretel” isn’t a witch at all but a baker feels like an earlier version of the story. I began to wish that Gidwitz would mention what his sources were when writing this tale. Because even if the baker idea was his own, it feels incredibly authentic.<br />	<br />Gidwitz, I should note, may seem to be adapting the Grimm tales in all their full gore, but he does make a couple alterations here and there. There are the obvious changes that have to be there for one tale to meld into another. The seven ravens are changed to the seven swallows since there are already three ravens of vast importance in this book, and any more would get confusing. And then there are the original elements that still aren’t quite appropriate for a middle grade novel. For example, in <i>A Tale Dark and Grimm</i> Johannes is instructed to bite the queen’s lip. In the original story, it’s her right breast. Ew. A good change then.<br />	<br />I was most intrigued when Gidwitz was at his most original. The story “Brother and Sister” seemingly has little to do with the original tale except that a boy and a girl are living on their own in a forest and the brother is turned into a wild beast. The story “A Smile As Red As Blood” seems closest to “The Robber Bridegroom”, complete with the telltale finger. It might be mixed with another story as well, though. The detail about killing warlocks by boiling them in oil with poisonous snakes felt a little too authentic. After reading for a while, you begin to find you cannot separate Gidwitz's writing from that of the Grimms. At the beginning of the book they are distinct and separate. The Grimms are almost word for word and Gidwitz just throws in a little snarky commentary. Then as the book progresses, more and more of Gidwitz seeps in so that by the end it’s impossible to say what is and isn’t authentic Grimm. Gidwitz’s technique will probably encourage kids to locate their own original Grimm tales. I recommend they lay their hands on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/826362.Grimm_s_Grimmest" title="Grimm's Grimmest by Brothers Grimm" rel="nofollow noopener">Grimm's Grimmest</a> complete with beautifully bloody illustrations by Tracy Dockray (best known for re-illustrating the "Ramona" books).<br />	<br />As for the violence, you can’t say Gidwitz doesn’t warn you. Indeed, before every gross, disgusting, or horrific passage (all authentically Grimm) he is careful to tell the reader things like, “Warning: this next bit is kind of gross” and “No little children around, right?” These stories have been around since long before the Grimms collected them during the early 19th century. Kids loved 'em in the past and from what I hear, kids today just eat this newest book up as well. The gore doesn’t get to them. It’s the parents who can’t take it. For a certain kind of child, this book will be the answer to their painless, bloodless, suburban lives. They’ll get sucked into this book early on and keep reading and reading until before they know it they’ve just finished a story with great writing and a bold theme. And when you talk it up to them you need only say one thing: “This book makes <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/125662.Say_Cheese_and_Die___Goosebumps___4_" title="Say Cheese and Die! (Goosebumps, #4) by R.L. Stine" rel="nofollow noopener">Goosebumps</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1325218.Scary_Stories_to_Tell_In_the_Dark" title="Scary Stories to Tell In the Dark by Alvin Schwartz" rel="nofollow noopener">Scary Stories to Tell in the Dark</a> look like pat-a-cake nursery rhymes.”<br />	<br />One does wonder if the narrator in this book isn’t a bit on the nose too often, though. The idea is to show not tell, but Gidwitz indulges in a fair amount of telling. His narrator is prone to saying things like, “Parents are supposed to help their children to grow wise and healthy and strong,” and “… Once Upon a Time, no grown-up was perfect. You, my dear reader, have certainly learned that by now.” He’s more than intrusive. He’s telling you the point of some of these tales, and adding observations of his own along the way. Some folks will be driven batty by this technique. Yet for me, the technique was so obvious from the start that I accepted it. I didn’t mind being told what one thing might mean or another. When you’re dealing with tales as upfront and brassy as the Grimm tales, a little contemporary commentary is more than welcome. This is a book for kids, after all.<br />	<br />Like a lot of middle grade novels out this year (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1999660.Cosmic" rel="nofollow noopener">Cosmic</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6609764.One_Crazy_Summer" title="One Crazy Summer by Rita Williams-Garcia" rel="nofollow noopener">One Crazy Summer</a>, etc.), <i>A Tale Dark and Grimm</i> is about parents and parenting. Says the narrator at one point, “It will happen to you, Dear Reader, at some point in your life. You will face a moment very much like the one Hansel and Gretel are facing right now. In this moment, you will look at your parents and realize that – no matter what it sounds like they are saying – they are actually asking you for forgiveness.” What is forgiveness, for that matter? How do you forgive people when they’ve done terrible things to you? Is there a point where you can let go, and is there harm in holding on to your anger? And how on earth do you take seven or more incredibly violent Grimm fairy tales and turn them into a meaningful story about finding home, finding yourself, and finding what it means to be forgiving? That Gidwitz attempted it in the first place is bizarre. That he succeeds is baffling. The good kind of baffling. With enough blood and guts to satisfy even the most craven of readers, this is the rare horror tale for kids that also happens to have a lot of literary merit as well. The combination crops up in young adult literature all the time, but not so much on the kid side of things. Such books are rarities. This book, a gem. A new idea for some very old literature. <br /><br />For ages 9-12.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16251806059422881113" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_292109978" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/292109978" />
    <a title="Melki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5293536-melki"><img alt="Melki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308071306p2/5293536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/292109978?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

  <span id="freeText4330651731749934275" style="display:none">Gidwitz spins a twisted tale that sends Hansel and Gretel into the deep, dark, and sometimes, bloody forest. Hansel has a Hell of a time, as heads roll, and dragons roar. Gretel's no slouch either, when it comes to taking names, and kicking butt. <br /><br />Anyone who enjoys their fairy tales on the grisly side should enjoy this story of two tough siblings and their grim adventures.</span>

  <span id="freeText17237807648820974228" style="display:none">[4 Stars] I actually finished this last week but am just now getting to this review. <div id="review_151522988" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151522988" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/355321-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472335580p2/355321.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151522988?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/355321-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/355321-heather?shelf=home-library">home-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151522988" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2246485615218825857">I studied fairy tales a bit in college -- one of my favorite subjects, in fact -- so the premise of this book intrigued me. Imagine if all those children in Grimm stories, the ones who pop up when a poor couple bemoans that they have no children, or who get entrapped by a creepy devil man, or who get killed by their parents, are actually the same two children. They're Hansel and Gretel. And each story, generally culled from the Grimms' work, takes them on a journey of self-discovery and independ</span>
  <span id="freeText2246485615218825857" style="display:none">I studied fairy tales a bit in college -- one of my favorite subjects, in fact -- so the premise of this book intrigued me. Imagine if all those children in Grimm stories, the ones who pop up when a poor couple bemoans that they have no children, or who get entrapped by a creepy devil man, or who get killed by their parents, are actually the same two children. They're Hansel and Gretel. And each story, generally culled from the Grimms' work, takes them on a journey of self-discovery and independence. Cool idea, yes? And it is! Unfortunately, the framework that holds the entire story together is a narrator who frequently makes interjections to warn the reader of impending doom. Perhaps in an effort to avoid sounding too Lemony Snickety, the tone of this narrator is excessively casual, jocular to the point of it being grating. I would've appreciated a more...genteel narrator ("Begging your pardon, gentle readers, but I simply must insist that..."). I frequently wished I could read faster just to skip over those bits and get back to the story of Hansel and Gretel, which I loved. Ultimately, I think my interest in this book was mostly due to the subject matter and less the execution/writing style. I'm not sure I'd seek out Gidwitz's next book, but I would be interested to know what he plans to tackle next, and if the subject appealed, I'd go for it.<br /><br />I will also admit that I'm an old softie so when I read the author's note in the back about how he's a second grade teacher, I melted and he endeared himself to me a bit more. You guys, I cry at things like shuttle launches and stories of old ladies who attend soldiers' funerals, so I can't be trusted.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2246485615218825857" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1712095194" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14786636127885580016">I would probably rate this one 3.5 but I would have lived for this book as a child. I loved that the author somehow managed to turn something that would normally be a book of different fairy tales, into that weaves them all together by following two young children through-out them all. It was very cleaver and really worked. The violence and gore is quite graphic for a middle-grade novel and I loved it and would've loved it as a kid. If your child is easily frightened then this might not be the b</span>
  <span id="freeText14786636127885580016" style="display:none">I would probably rate this one 3.5 but I would have lived for this book as a child. I loved that the author somehow managed to turn something that would normally be a book of different fairy tales, into that weaves them all together by following two young children through-out them all. It was very cleaver and really worked. The violence and gore is quite graphic for a middle-grade novel and I loved it and would've loved it as a kid. If your child is easily frightened then this might not be the book for them though. Fun stuff and I plan on continuing the series. <br /><br />RTC</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2448828470" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17561660415068250857"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1513367806i/24684994._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b> 3.5 stars </b><br/><br/><b> <i> “You see, to find the brightest wisdom one must pass through the darkest zones. And through the darkest zones there can be no guide. <br/>No guide, that is, but courage” </i> </b><br/><br/>This is probably one of the most disturbing books I've ever read, and it's a children's book. That being said, I think this is perfect for the right child, but it definitely not for the faint of heart. A retelling of stories from the Grimm brothers, this book focuses mostly on the dark tales of Hansel and Gretel. There </span>
  <span id="freeText17561660415068250857" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1513367806i/24684994._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> 3.5 stars </b><br><br><b> <i> “You see, to find the brightest wisdom one must pass through the darkest zones. And through the darkest zones there can be no guide. <br>No guide, that is, but courage” </i> </b><br><br>This is probably one of the most disturbing books I've ever read, and it's a children's book. That being said, I think this is perfect for the right child, but it definitely not for the faint of heart. A retelling of stories from the Grimm brothers, this book focuses mostly on the dark tales of Hansel and Gretel. There is more to their stories than what we thought, and Gidwitz is telling them all.<br><br><b> <i> “You see, Hansel and Gretel don’t just show up at the end of this story.<br><br>They show up.<br><br>And then they get their heads cut off.<br><br>Just thought you’d like to know.” </i> </b><br><br>I thought the narrative voice in this novel was amazingly done and hysterical. The stories themselves were interesting and compelling. What makes it a 3.5 for me, is this book was way too violent and disturbed for my liking. I enjoyed the book for the most part, but apparently I'm a massive wimp and it was a tad too much for me.<br><br><b> <i> “There is a wisdom in children, a kind of knowing, a kind of believing, that we, as adults, do not have. There is a time when a kingdom needs its children.” </i> </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1494101706i/22685352._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Follow me on ♥ <a href="http://www.facebook.com/rachelreadsravenously" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> ♥ <a href="http://rachelsreadsravenously.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> ♥ <a href="http://instagram.com/rachelreadsravenously" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ♥ <a href="https://twitter.com/rayliz89" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ♥<br></span>

<div id="review_143190499" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/143190499" />
    <a title="Chris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/379992-chris"><img alt="Chris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1208745186p2/379992.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/143190499?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris" href="/user/show/379992-chris">Chris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/379992-chris?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/379992-chris?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/379992-chris?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/379992-chris?shelf=not-graphic">not-graphic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/379992-chris?shelf=j">j</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/379992-chris?shelf=legends-and-lore">legends-and-lore</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer143190499" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7075853850197171542">I've always liked an analogy for reading I once heard from an English teacher: sometimes your relationship with a book can be just like relationships with people. There are people you'll be instantly drawn to because they have a particular charisma or chemistry for you, yet with time you might realize they lack the depth and quality to be a good relationship. And there are people who don't immediately impress you or draw you in, but the more time you spend getting to know them the more they grow</span>
  <span id="freeText7075853850197171542" style="display:none">I've always liked an analogy for reading I once heard from an English teacher: sometimes your relationship with a book can be just like relationships with people. There are people you'll be instantly drawn to because they have a particular charisma or chemistry for you, yet with time you might realize they lack the depth and quality to be a good relationship. And there are people who don't immediately impress you or draw you in, but the more time you spend getting to know them the more they grow on you until one day you realize how awesome they are and how much you value your relationship with them. She usually shared this with students who were ready to dismiss a good book too quickly, to encourage them to keep reading, but I've found it's good advice in the reverse instance, too.<br /><br />I absolutely loved the introduction to this book, for instance, and instantly assumed it would be great. Then I had to get through a period of disappointment in the middle of the book as I kept reading and realized the device was only good for so much and could get tiresome rather quickly. Luckily, I kept reading even longer until I got to the end and my final assessment is somewhere in the middle.<br /><br />The device is a snarky, intrusive narrator--somewhere in the mix between Lemony Snicket and the grampa in The Princess Bride (film)--who keeps telling us just how awful and gruesome (and clever) his tales are:<br /><br /><i>Once upon a time, fairy tales were awesome.<br /><br />I know, I know. You don't believe me. I don't blame you. A little while ago, I wouldn't have believed it myself. Little girls in red caps skipping around the forest? Awesome? I don't think so.<br /><br />But then I started to read them. The real, Grimm ones. Very few little girls in red caps in those.<br /><br />Well, there's one. But she gets eaten. . . . <br /><br />Before I go on, a word of warning: Grimm's stories--the ones that weren't changed for little kids--are violent and bloody. And what you're going to hear now, the one true tale in </i>The Tales of Grimm,<i> is as violent and bloody as you can imagine.<br /><br />Really.<br /><br />So if such things bother you, we should probably stop right now.<br /><br />You see, the land of Grimm can be a harrowing place. But it is worth exploring. For, in life, it is in the darkest zones one finds the brightest beauty and the most luminous wisdom.<br /><br />And, of course, the most blood.</i><br /><br />That's the start and end of the introduction. What I left out describes the bulk of the book--which is not the narrator but the tales themselves. They are a number of the traditional Grimm tales reworked a bit so they all feature Hansel and Gretel as protagonists to make one larger, ongoing story. The original tone, structure, and style is largely preserved, so the storytelling doesn't focus so much on voice or realism or character as most books do; but it's effective for the source material and if you give things enough of a chance you find those things are there, just in subtle, slow developing ways. This was a fun, worthwhile read in the end, just not quite in the way I expected after reading just the introduction.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7075853850197171542" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_634671979" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/634671979" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4255477-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398251387p2/4255477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/634671979?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/4255477-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10533544-a-tale-dark-and-grimm">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=emily">emily</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=fairy-tale-like">fairy-tale-like</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer634671979" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10337341313951829087">3.7 Stars<br/><br/>I don't know about you, but Hansel and Gretel was always one of my least favorite fairy tales. They were always so naive, and it felt like they made it out the other side based on chance, and not any particular skill or growth they'd experienced. Here, not so. Here, Adam Gidwitz has imagined a tale that's much longer than the one we know, much more involved, and is actually several shorter tales woven together to tell the whole tale - dark and grimm.<br/><br/><blockquote><br/>You see, Hansel and Gretel don't just</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText10337341313951829087" style="display:none">3.7 Stars<br /><br />I don't know about you, but Hansel and Gretel was always one of my least favorite fairy tales. They were always so naive, and it felt like they made it out the other side based on chance, and not any particular skill or growth they'd experienced. Here, not so. Here, Adam Gidwitz has imagined a tale that's much longer than the one we know, much more involved, and is actually several shorter tales woven together to tell the whole tale - dark and grimm.<br /><br /><blockquote><br />You see, Hansel and Gretel don't just <i>show up</i> at the end of this story.<br /><br />They show up.<br /><br />And then they get their heads cut off.<br /><br />Just thought you'd like to know.</blockquote><br /><br />This was, simply, one of the most fun, interesting, and AWESOME retellings I've ever read. I was immediately hooked from the small sample that I read, engaged by Gidwitz's asides to the reader throughout. He's irreverent, snarky, slightly callous, and more than somewhat tactless - and I LOVE it. Beyond his commentary, there's a wonderful ease to the writing of the fairy tales. The voice is simple enough to read aloud to children - though the author warns there are parts that may not be appropriate for them - and fun enough that the whole family will enjoy it.<br /><br /><blockquote><br />Before I go on, a word of warning: Grimm's stories--the ones that weren't changed for little kids--are violent and bloody. And what you're going to hear now, the one true tale in <i>The Tales of Grimm</i>, is as violent and bloody as you can imagine.<br /><br />Really.<br /><br />So if such things both you, we should probably stop right now.<br /><br />You see, the land of Grimm can be a harrowing place. But it is worth exploring. For, in life, it is in the darkest zones one finds the brightest beauty and the most luminous wisdom.<br /><br />And, of course, the most blood.</blockquote><br /><br />One of the best things about this expanded tale of Hansel and Gretel is that the characters actually go through quite a lot of growth. We start the (overall) story before they're even born, and go through many adventures with them. Their growth and changes are so subtle that I barely noticed it was happening. Each small experience served to make them stronger, smarter, and more compassionate. Though they are still typical fairy tale characters, there is a lot more personality there than I was expecting.<br /><br /><blockquote><br />There is a certain kind of pain that can change you. Even the strongest sword, when placed in a raging fire, will soften and bend and change its form.</blockquote><br /><br />This book was a real treat. Fun, silly, bloody, and true to the fairy tale form. I'm definitely looking forward to more from Adam Gidwitz and I'm glad I've got the next two books in the series already on my Kindle.<br /><br /><blockquote><br />Once upon a time, fairy tales were awesome. <br /><br />I know, I know. You don't believe me. I don't blame you. A little while ago, I wouldn't have believed it myself....<br /><br />You know how it is with stories. Someone tells a story. Then someone repeats it and it changes. Someone else repeats it, and it changes again. Then someone's telling it to their kid and taking out all the scar, bloody scenes--in other words, the awesome parts--and the next thing you know the story's about an adorable little girl in a red cap, skipping through the forest to take cookies to her granny. And you're so bored you've passed out on the floor.</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="10337341313951829087" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1960895631" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

I recommend this book to anyone!! The one thing I didn't like was in some chapters I felt like they should have add more information, because at times I felt it ended so fast with no information. Overall this book is g</span>
  <span id="freeText2921550392625929086" style="display:none">Okay, I hate traditional literature books, but this was a fabulous book! I loved it! I liked how the author took a simple story of two characters that everyone knows and turned into an amazing detailed, action book! It was a book you want to keep reading to see what happened next. I recommend this book to anyone!! The one thing I didn't like was in some chapters I felt like they should have add more information, because at times I felt it ended so fast with no information. Overall this book is great!</span>

<div id="review_151711690" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151711690" />
    <a title="Dolly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1019021-dolly"><img alt="Dolly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1223325529p2/1019021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151711690?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dolly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dolly" href="/user/show/1019021-dolly">Dolly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">parents reading with their children</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=scifi-fantasy">scifi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=short-stories-essays">short-stories-essays</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=germany">germany</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=lorton-jammin-book-party">lorton-jammin-book-party</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1019021-dolly?shelf=cooking-recipes">cooking-recipes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151711690" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9118199707287989780">It took us a long time to read this book. Since we hadn't finished by the time it was due back at the library, we had to return it before we finished as there were holds on it. So we put it on hold again ourselves and promised to finish it as soon as we could. <br/><br/>It was a great book, filled with fantastic and action-filled stories that were gruesome, but exciting. I have read some about children's ability to detach the written story from reality and be relatively unaffected by gore (more so than wi</span>
  <span id="freeText9118199707287989780" style="display:none">It took us a long time to read this book. Since we hadn't finished by the time it was due back at the library, we had to return it before we finished as there were holds on it. So we put it on hold again ourselves and promised to finish it as soon as we could. <br /><br />It was a great book, filled with fantastic and action-filled stories that were gruesome, but exciting. I have read some about children's ability to detach the written story from reality and be relatively unaffected by gore (more so than with movies and other visual media.) And I believe it. <br /><br />Our youngest got a bit alarmed in some parts, but mainly I think she got bored by the sheer length of the book. But our oldest was enraptured by this book and we read the last 112 pages all at once, with her urging me to read more at the end of every story. And neither has complained of nightmares, so that's good! <br /><br />I love that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3407883.Adam_Gidwitz" title="Adam Gidwitz" rel="nofollow noopener">Adam Gidwitz</a> remained true to the tales, reworking them only to fit the context of the overall tale and not deeming it necessary to censor the blook and violence. I love that the stories are old, yet feel timeless. <br /><br />And best of all, I love the comic asides that breathe a little bit of levity into the tale, especially as things start to get grim (ha ha.) Overall, it was a terrific book and we really enjoyed reading the stories together.<br /><br />February 2012 update: Our oldest really, <u>really</u> likes this book. She often mentions it as her favorite story. I love that this book has had such an impact on her, since we read this book almost a year ago, and her long-term memory for many of the books we've read together is not all that good. She even chose this book as her selection to read aloud to the class when she was "Super Kid" in her third-grade class the week of 30 Jan - 3 Feb 2012. I discussed the book with her teacher, who was a bit concerned at first, but was okay with the short bit that she read aloud. <br /><br />interesting quote:<br /><i>"...there is a wisdom in children, a kind of knowing, a kind of believing, that we, as adults, do not have. There is a time when a kingdom needs its children. These children." (p. 245)</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9118199707287989780" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_576650719" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/576650719" />
    <a title="Kendra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5971941-kendra"><img alt="Kendra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1399500470p2/5971941.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/576650719?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kendra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kendra" href="/user/show/5971941-kendra">Kendra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789790244771" href="/book/show/11974615-a-tale-dark-and-grimm">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer576650719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14879525654607726210">I wanted to like this book – honestly, I did! The premise is intriguing, and I love fairy tales. Plus it garnered so many glowing reviews that I kept cutting it a bit more slack than I otherwise would have done.<br/><br/>But I found the book to be both dull and irritating. What truly turned me off to this book was the thinness of the plot and the intrusiveness of the narrator. As others have noted, Lemony Snicket this is not -- not even Book 13 Lemony Snicket!<br/><br/>I loved the original tales, so the violence wa</span>
  <span id="freeText14879525654607726210" style="display:none">I wanted to like this book – honestly, I did! The premise is intriguing, and I love fairy tales. Plus it garnered so many glowing reviews that I kept cutting it a bit more slack than I otherwise would have done.<br /><br />But I found the book to be both dull and irritating. What truly turned me off to this book was the thinness of the plot and the intrusiveness of the narrator. As others have noted, Lemony Snicket this is not -- not even Book 13 Lemony Snicket!<br /><br />I loved the original tales, so the violence wasn't troubling to me. Sure, I wouldn’t have read it to my kids when they were very small, but there's plenty of bad stuff in Disney stories, and they learnt at a young age to avoid any book or movie with a dog as the main character's best friend after one of their 3rd grade teachers read them Old Yeller and Sounder. (Was that ever traumatic for ME!) In a nutshell, I think it’s important for you to know your kids and what they can handle. <br /><br />So go try the original Grimm stories!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14879525654607726210" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1219732724?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1219732724" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3826667724382411580">This is an odd book...short with a "young" cover painting the book is played for somewhat adult humor played against the back drop of the "original" morality tales (bloody morality tales) told in the Grim Grimm's Fairy Tales. You know the ones where the step sisters try cutting off their toes and then their heels to make them fit in the glass slipper? <br/><br/>Here we're told a story of Hansel and Gretel...but not the one you're familiar with. No with repeated warnings to be sure there are no children in</span>
  <span id="freeText3826667724382411580" style="display:none">This is an odd book...short with a "young" cover painting the book is played for somewhat adult humor played against the back drop of the "original" morality tales (bloody morality tales) told in the Grim Grimm's Fairy Tales. You know the ones where the step sisters try cutting off their toes and then their heels to make them fit in the glass slipper? <br /><br />Here we're told a story of Hansel and Gretel...but not the one you're familiar with. No with repeated warnings to be sure there are no children in the room we're told a series of adventures from the viewpoint of our young heroes...<br /><br />Not a bad book, as a matter of fact a pretty good book. I think I'll plan on getting the next in the series...<br /><br />What? Yes of course it's a series, isn't everything "now-a-days"? </span>
  <a data-text-id="3826667724382411580" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2774441016" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2774441016" />
    <a title="Shannara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32384337-shannara"><img alt="Shannara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601562645p2/32384337.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2774441016?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannara" href="/user/show/32384337-shannara">Shannara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2774441016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12231867989662719670">So that was a little dark and Grimm... but in the best way possible! This was such an entertaining book! It grabbed my attention from the start and just wouldn’t let go. This wove together some fairy tales in a way to make them something new and seriously fun. There is quite a bit of gore, but what would a Grimm tale be without some blood here and there. Hansel and Gretel are such great protagonists and I love reading about their troubles and growth. I definitely recommend this to those who like</span>
  <span id="freeText12231867989662719670" style="display:none">So that was a little dark and Grimm... but in the best way possible! This was such an entertaining book! It grabbed my attention from the start and just wouldn’t let go. This wove together some fairy tales in a way to make them something new and seriously fun. There is quite a bit of gore, but what would a Grimm tale be without some blood here and there. Hansel and Gretel are such great protagonists and I love reading about their troubles and growth. I definitely recommend this to those who like Grimm style tales, a little twisted, kinda sick, but totally entertaining. </span>

<div id="review_1963544117" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1963544117" />
    <a title="George Jankovic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48492241-george-jankovic"><img alt="George Jankovic" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492530766p2/48492241.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1963544117?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="George Jankovic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="George Jankovic" href="/user/show/48492241-george-jankovic">George Jankovic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1963544117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer892642649192995773">5 stars for this novel. The author takes a bunch of Grimm brothers' tales--not what you think they are, but the original, bloody ones--and weaves them into one story in which Hansel and Gretel are the protagonists. Then he inserts himself--the narrator--into the story from time to time with wonderful humor.<br/><br/>For example, he will ask whether any "little kids" are still in the room if some gory scenes are coming. Or will just make a funny interjection. <br/><br/>The hapless kids in this story go through a lot</span>
  <span id="freeText892642649192995773" style="display:none">5 stars for this novel. The author takes a bunch of Grimm brothers' tales--not what you think they are, but the original, bloody ones--and weaves them into one story in which Hansel and Gretel are the protagonists. Then he inserts himself--the narrator--into the story from time to time with wonderful humor.<br /><br />For example, he will ask whether any "little kids" are still in the room if some gory scenes are coming. Or will just make a funny interjection. <br /><br />The hapless kids in this story go through a lot of grief and suffering, which changes them profoundly.<br /><br />5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="892642649192995773" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer629023839" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8887296126598174692">I try to hold back the five star rating for the truly special books that I read. This one is deserving of at least five stars. This retelling of Hansel and Gretel and the Grimm Tales. You might think that a retelling aimed at the 9-12 year old set would hold back, but that's not the case. It's dark, bloody, and even manages some laugh out loud humor throughout. I believe this one is meant to be read aloud - if you get a chance, try it. The wry and funny asides from the narrator made me laugh out</span>
  <span id="freeText8887296126598174692" style="display:none">I try to hold back the five star rating for the truly special books that I read. This one is deserving of at least five stars. This retelling of Hansel and Gretel and the Grimm Tales. You might think that a retelling aimed at the 9-12 year old set would hold back, but that's not the case. It's dark, bloody, and even manages some laugh out loud humor throughout. I believe this one is meant to be read aloud - if you get a chance, try it. The wry and funny asides from the narrator made me laugh out loud a few times, and I really was a bit sad for this one to end. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1Ak9lLsi74q+1qW4FeU41dQwk/fmHlK82M7Y/jbmjUi/I+VAQhOVRqeSjf+IoOCIzTvqpM9WudxUzGYSmWFRRg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+Fe8qs49oou+MP3hLxfzjtMHOMPA+n5Vw1etnhgd7lyTfWR+NwzYR6d01aayUivTygxBkOmylTVPVRNyt5oyUg==')})
  }
//]]>

One step closer to losing the things she cares about the most.\n \nFor a while, the only thing that keeps Hailey moving forward is the feeling she gets when she crosses something off the list. \n\nThen she meets Kyle. He mumbles—when he talks at all—and listens to music to drown out his thoughts. He’s loaded down with fears, too. So Hailey talks him into making his own list.\n \nTogether, they stumble into an odd friendship, helping each other tackle one after another of their biggest fears. But fate and timing can change everything. And sometimes facing your worst fear makes you realize you had nothing to lose after all.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"11572845785831268472\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return
